## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics â€” nonlinear oscillations & dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, matching second-order ODE models for (nonlinear) harmonic oscillators with restoring forces, damping, and external/parametric forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (simple) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (pure linear restoring force, no damping/forcing)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized damped oscillator)
- Constant + linear terms (bias/offset): dv_dt = c0 - c1 * x - c2 * v (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Driven (sinusoidal forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (externally forced oscillator)
- Driven (cosinusoidal forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (alternative forcing phase convention)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order stiffness (cubicâ€“quintic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (angle-like coordinate with sinusoidal restoring torque)
- Quadratic/cubic drag (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag contribution)
- Nonlinear stiffness with piecewise-like odd symmetry: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (stiffness increases with |x|)
- Van der Pol oscillator (negative damping near origin): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited limit-cycle oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent pumping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (another self-excited oscillator form)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * x - c4 * v (Mathieu-type parametrically excited oscillator)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)
- Saturating/nonlinear restoring force (softening): dv_dt = -c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) - c2 * v (restoring force weakens at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative symmetric oscillators often have dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3, -sin(c*x)); even-in-x terms can indicate bias/asymmetry or shifted equilibrium.
- Damping symmetry: physical dissipation typically gives a term odd in v (e.g., -v, -v*Abs(v), -(a + b*x**2)*v); even-in-v damping terms are usually nonphysical unless modeling control/rectification.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: factors like (c1 - x**2)*v or (c1 - v**2)*v indicate negative damping for small amplitude and positive damping for large amplitude, producing stable oscillations.
- External driving identification: additive sin(c*t+phi) or cos(c*t+phi) terms suggest forcing independent of state; harmonics (sin(k*t)) imply multi-frequency drive.
- Parametric resonance signature: time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v), such as (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicate parametric excitation (Mathieu-like behavior).
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: dominant +x**3 (within dv_dt = -x - x**3 ...) yields amplitude-dependent frequency hardening; dominant -x**3 (i.e., dv_dt = -x + c*x**3 ...) yields softening.
- Nonlinear drag regimes: presence of v*Abs(v) (or higher powers like v**3) indicates high-Reynolds-number or nonlinear damping where decay rate depends on speed.
- Potential-driven structure: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), it suggests conservative motion with dv_dt = -dU/dx for some potential U(x); adding v terms breaks energy conservation.
- Amplitude-limited restoring force: rational forms like x/(c + x**2) or sin(c*x) suggest bounded force for large |x|, often modeling geometric constraints or saturation of restoring torque.

GT: -beta*sin(v) - omega0**c0*(gamma*t + c1)*x - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 2.5126990598325*x*(0.0921849151045819*t + 1) - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-2.5126990598325*x**3 - 0.231655455*t*x - 2.5126990598325*x - 0.774919680656294*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `t*x`
3. `x**3`
4. `sin(v)`

The key challenge: `sin(v)` is a specific basis function. Candidates use combinations of `v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, etc. The question is whether `sin(v)` can be exactly represented by these terms.

**Critical observation:** `sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by any finite polynomial in `v`, nor by `v + v*Abs(v) + v**3` or similar combinations. These are fundamentally different basis functions. `sin(v)` is transcendental and linearly independent from all polynomial/piecewise-polynomial functions of `v`.

Let me check if ANY candidate contains `sin(v)` or an equivalent:

Looking through all candidates:
- Candidate 35 has `sin(c4*v + c5)` â€” this could match `sin(v)` with `c4=1, c5=0`.
- Candidate 43 has `cos(c8*t + c9)` â€” this involves `t`, not `v`.

Almost all candidates use `v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3` as their `v`-dependent terms. Since `sin(v)` is NOT equivalent to any combination of `v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `v**5`, etc. (by linear independence of polynomial and transcendental functions), these candidates cannot match.

**Candidate 35:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*log(c3*Abs(v) + 1)*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6*x**3 + c7*t*x + c8*v*Abs(v) + c9*v**3`

This has `sin(v)` available (via `c4=1, c5=0`), but it's multiplied by `log(c3*Abs(v) + 1)`. Setting `c3=0` gives `log(1)*sin(v) = 0`. So we can't isolate `sin(v)` from this term. We'd need `log(c3*Abs(v)+1)` to be constant, which requires `c3=0`, making the whole term zero. So this can't produce a pure `sin(v)` term. The remaining `v`-terms (`c1*v + c8*v*Abs(v) + c9*v**3`) can't represent `sin(v)`.

Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]

For ALL other candidates (1-34, 36-50): None contain `sin(v)` or any trigonometric function of `v`. They all use polynomial-like functions of `v` (`v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `Abs(v)`, etc.), which cannot exactly equal `sin(v)` for all `v`. By the principle of linear independence of transcendental and algebraic functions, no finite combination of these can equal `sin(v)`.

Candidate 43 has `cos(c8*t + c9)` which is a function of `t`, not `v`, so it can't produce `sin(v)`.

Therefore, **no candidate matches the GT**.
